# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox DOM Event Dispatch Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a DOM event (e.g., click) is dispatched through the Firefox event system in mozilla/gecko-dev. Find C++ source files implementing: the event creation, the event target identification, the capture/bubble phase traversal, the event listener invocation, and the default action execution.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/firefox--871325b8.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

43-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of the Firefox DOM event dispatch system. The answer file at `/workspace/answer.json` documents the complete event dispatch chain in Firefox's C++ implementation.

## Summary of Key Findings:

The Firefox event dispatch system flows through these main stages:

1. **Event Creation** - `EventDispatcher::CreateEvent()` wraps widget events as DOM events
2. **Event Target Chain Building** - `EventDispatcher::Dispatch()` walks the DOM tree via `GetEventTargetParent()` to build an array of target items
3. **Capture Phase** - Dispatched from root to target through `EventTargetChainItem::HandleEventTargetChain()`
4. **Target Phase** - Listeners at both capture and bubble on the target element fire
5. **Bubble Phase** - Dispatches from target parent back up to root
6. **Event Listener Invocation** - `EventListenerManager::HandleEventSingleListener()` invokes each listener's callback
7. **Default Action Execution** - `ActivationBehavior()` runs element-specific default behaviors (form submission, checkbox toggle, etc.)

The key files identified are:
- **dom/events/EventDispatcher.h/cpp** - Core dispatch logic
- **dom/events/EventListenerManager.h/cpp** - Listener management and invocation  
- **dom/events/EventTarget.h** - Base event target interface
- **widget/BasicEvents.h** - Widget event definitions
- **layout/base/PresShell.cpp** - PresShell integration
- **dom/html/HTMLButtonElement.cpp**, **HTMLInputElement.cpp** - Default action implementations

Target Phase (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp:587-611)\\n\\n**Target Item Handling:**\\n- Sets `mInTargetPhase = true` (line 588)\\n- Calls `HandleEvent()` twice: once in capture mode, then again in bubble mode (lines 598, 605)\\n- This allows listeners with `capture:true` and `capture:false` to both fire on the target element\\n- Handles `PostHandleEvent` for system group (line 609)\\n\\n### 5. Bubble Phase (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp:613-648)\\n\\n**Phase Setup (lines 600-601):**\\n```cpp\\naVisitor.mEvent->mFlags.mInCapturePhase = false;\\naVisitor.mEvent->mFlags.mInBubblingPhase = true;\\n```\\n\\n**Iteration (lines 614-647):**\\n- Iterates forward from target's parent to root\\n- Only processes items if `mBubbles` flag is set or event needs retargeting (line 638)\\n- Calls `HandleEvent()` for bubbling listeners (line 642)\\n\\n### 6. Event Listener Invocation (dom/events/EventListenerManager.cpp:1439-1534)\\n\\n**Main Entry Point - HandleEventInternal():**\\n- Sets up context for listener execution (lines 1460-1467)\\n- Finds listeners for the event type atom (lines 1481-1517)\\n- Handles both \\\"all events\\\" listeners and type-specific listeners\\n\\n**Listener Array Processing - HandleEventWithListenerArray() (lines 1536-1627):**\\n- Lazily creates DOM event if needed (lines 1540-1551)\\n- Iterates through listeners matching the event phase (lines 1558-1593)\\n- For each listener:\\n  - Checks phase matching: `listener->MatchesEventPhase(aEvent)` (line 1567)\\n  - Validates event trustedness (line 1568)\\n  - Handles \\\"once\\\" listeners by moving them before invocation (lines 1573-1580)\\n\\n**Single Listener Invocation - HandleEventSingleListener() (lines 1233-1295):**\\n- Sets `aEvent->mCurrentTarget` to the current target (lines 1236-1240)\\n- Sets passive listener flag (line 1243)\\n- For WebIDL callbacks: calls `callback->HandleEvent(aCurrentTarget, *aDOMEvent, rv)` (lines 1276-1277)\\n- For XPCOM callbacks: calls `callback->HandleEvent(aDOMEvent)` (line 1282)\\n- Sets exception flag if listener throws (line 1291)\\n- Returns whether propagation should continue (line 1294)\\n\\n### 7. Default Action Execution (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp:446-489)\\n\\n**Activation Behavior Chain Item Methods:**\\n\\n**LegacyPreActivationBehavior() (lines 446-453):**\\n- Called before listeners on elements that want activation behavior\\n- Allows elements to suppress default behavior or modify event state\\n\\n**ActivationBehavior() (lines 466-472):**\\n- Called after event listeners have been invoked (in system event group)\\n- For HTMLButtonElement (HTMLButtonElement.cpp:315-349): submits form if in form\\n- For HTMLInputElement (HTMLInputElement.cpp): varies by input type (checkbox toggles, radio selects, submit/reset submits)\\n- Copies `mItemFlags` and `mItemData` to visitor for element-specific processing\\n\\n**PostHandleEvent() (lines 483-489):**\\n- Final post-processing for each chain item\\n- Allows elements to clean up or perform final actions\\n\\n### 8. System Event Group Dispatch (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp:651-693)\\n\\n**System Group Handling:**\\n- First dispatches to default event group (content listeners)\\n- If event allows system group (line 652), resets propagation flags and retargets\\n- Calls callback if provided (line 671) - allows PresShell to handle default actions\\n- Re-runs entire dispatch chain for system group listeners\\n- System group is protected from content script interference\\n\\n### 9. Integration Points\\n\\n**PresShell Integration (layout/base/PresShell.cpp:9099-9101):**\\n- `PresShell::EventHandler::DispatchEvent()` bridges between widget system and DOM\\n- Converts native widget events to DOM events\\n- Provides default action handling through `EventDispatchingCallback`\\n\\n**Widget Events (widget/BasicEvents.h:637-875):**\\n- Core `WidgetEvent` class with message type, flags, and target information\\n- Flags control dispatch behavior: `mBubbles`, `mCancelable`, `mInCapturePhase`, etc.\\n- Methods: `DefaultPrevented()`, `PreventDefault()`, `StopPropagation()`\\n\\n**Event Messages (widget/EventMessageList.h):**\\n- Defines all event types: eMouseClick, eTouchStart, eKeyDown, etc.\\n- Organized by event class and category\\n\\n### Complete Event Lifecycle Summary\\n\\n1. **Creation**: WidgetEvent created with message type and target\\n2. **DOM Event Wrapper**: Created on demand from WidgetEvent\\n3. **Chain Building**: Walk DOM tree from target to root via GetEventTargetParent()\\n4. **Capture Phase**: Dispatch from root to target, capture listeners only\\n5. **Target Phase**: Dispatch to target element, both capture and bubble listeners\\n6. **Bubble Phase**: Dispatch from target parent to root, bubble listeners only\\n7. **System Group**: Repeat phases 4-6 for system listeners after default group\\n8. **Activation Behavior**: Execute default action (form submission, checkbox toggle, etc.)\\n9. **Post-Processing**: Element-specific cleanup via PostHandleEvent()\\n\\nThis architecture ensures complete separation between content and system events, proper event phase handling, shadow DOM support with retargeting, and clean default action execution following the DOM specification.\"\n}\n",
